\hbox{{\bf  Classes}}
\entityintro{HistoryMetricsAction}{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.actions.HistoryMetricsAction}{Our sample action implements workbench action delegate.}
\vskip .1in
\vskip .1in
\subsection{\label{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.actions.HistoryMetricsAction}Class HistoryMetricsAction}{
\hypertarget{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.actions.HistoryMetricsAction}{}\vskip .1in 
Our sample action implements workbench action delegate. The action proxy will be created by the workbench and shown in the UI. When the user tries to use the action, this delegate will be created and execution will be delegated to it.\vskip .1in 
\subsubsection{See also}{}

  \begin{list}{-- }{\setlength{\itemsep}{0cm}\setlength{\parsep}{0cm}}
\item{ IWorkbenchWindowActionDelegate} 
  \end{list}
\subsubsection{Declaration}{
\small public class HistoryMetricsAction
\\ {\bf  extends} java.lang.Object
\refdefined{java.lang.Object}}
\subsubsection{Constructor summary}{
\begin{verse}
\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.actions.HistoryMetricsAction()}{{\bf HistoryMetricsAction()}} The constructor.\\
\end{verse}
}
\subsubsection{Method summary}{
\begin{verse}
\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.actions.HistoryMetricsAction.dispose()}{{\bf dispose()}} We can use this method to dispose of any system resources we previously allocated.\\
\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.actions.HistoryMetricsAction.init(IWorkbenchWindow)}{{\bf init(IWorkbenchWindow)}} We will cache window object in order to be able to provide parent shell for the message dialog.\\
\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.actions.HistoryMetricsAction.run(IAction)}{{\bf run(IAction)}} The action has been activated.\\
\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.actions.HistoryMetricsAction.selectionChanged(IAction, ISelection)}{{\bf selectionChanged(IAction, ISelection)}} Selection in the workbench has been changed.\\
\end{verse}

\section{Package it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan}{
\label{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan}\hypertarget{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan}{}
\hskip -.05in
\hbox to \hsize{\textit{ Package Contents\hfil Page}}
\vskip .13in
\hbox{{\bf  Classes}}
\entityintro{ChangePoint}{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.ChangePoint}{An implementation of \hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.db.entities.Change}{}{\small 
\refdefined{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.db.entities.Change}} for points with integer coordinates A single \hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.ChangePoint}{}{\small 
\refdefined{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.ChangePoint}} has two instance variables, a \hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.db.entities.Change}{}{\small 
\refdefined{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.db.entities.Change}} instance and an integer coordinate}
\entityintro{Cluster}{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.Cluster}{Cluster holding a set of points}
\entityintro{DBSCAN}{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.DBSCAN}{DBSCAN (density-based spatial clustering of applications with noise) algorithm

The DBSCAN algorithm forms clusters based on the idea of density connectivity, i.e. a point p is density connected to another point q, if there exists a chain of points p$_{i}$, with i=1...n and p$_{1}$=p and p$_{n}$=q, such that each pair p$_{i+1}$ is directly density-reachable from p$_{i}$.}
\vskip .1in
\vskip .1in

\subsection{\label{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.DBSCAN}Class DBSCAN}{
\hypertarget{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.DBSCAN}{}\vskip .1in 
DBSCAN (density-based spatial clustering of applications with noise) algorithm

The DBSCAN algorithm forms clusters based on the idea of density connectivity, i.e. a point p is density connected to another point q, if there exists a chain of points p$_{i}$, with i=1...n and p$_{1}$=p and p$_{n}$=q, such that each pair p$_{i+1}$ is directly density-reachable from p$_{i}$. A point q is directly density-reachable from point p if it is in the $\epsilon$-neighborhood or this point.

Any point that is not density-reachable from a formed cluster is treated as noise, and will thus not be present in the results.

The algorithm requires two parameters:\begin{itemize}
\item{\vskip -.8ex eps: the distance that defines the}
\item{\vskip -.8ex epsilon-neighborhood of a point minPoints: the minimum number of density-connected points required to form a cluster}
\end{itemize}
\vskip .1in 
\subsubsection{Declaration}{
\small public class DBSCAN
\\ {\bf  extends} java.lang.Object
\refdefined{java.lang.Object}}
\subsubsection{Constructor summary}{
\begin{verse}
\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.DBSCAN(double, int)}{{\bf DBSCAN(double, int)}} Creates a new instance of a DBSCAN\\
\end{verse}
}
\subsubsection{Method summary}{
\begin{verse}
\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.dbscan.DBSCAN.cluster(java.util.List)}{{\bf cluster(List)}} Perform DBSCAN cluster analysis\\

\end{verse}

\index{getECCModificationBased(Project, int, boolean)}

\texttt{public java.util.List\ {\bf  getECCModificationBased}(\texttt{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.db.entities.Project} {\bf  pProject},
\texttt{int} {\bf  pLimit},
\texttt{boolean} {\bf  pIsStatic}) throws it.unisa.sesa.repominer.metrics.exception.NoChangesException
\label{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.metrics.ProjectMetrics.getECCModificationBased(it.unisa.sesa.repominer.db.entities.Project, int, boolean)}}%end signature
\begin{itemize}
\item{
{\bf  Description}

This method calculate a set of values of ECC Model using modification limit period based; it calculates this values broken the history of changes into period based on number of modifications specified in preferences panel. To prevent a period where little development may have occurred from spanning a long time, we impose a limit of 3 months on a period even if the modification limit was no reached
}
\item{
{\bf  Parameters}
  \begin{itemize}
   \item{
\texttt{pProject} -- project analyzed}
   \item{
\texttt{pLimit} -- limit of modifications for breaking periods}
   \item{
\texttt{pIsStatic} -- if true calculated with Normalized Static Entropy; if false calculated with our Adaptive Sizing Entropy}
  \end{itemize}
}%end item
\item{{\bf  Returns} -- 
some ECC Model value calculated with modification limit period method 
}%end item
\end{itemize}
}%end item

\subsection{\label{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.preferences.PreferencePage}Class PreferencePage}{
\hypertarget{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.preferences.PreferencePage}{}\vskip .1in 
This class represents a preference page that is contributed to the Preferences dialog. By subclassing FieldEditorPreferencePage, we can use the field support built into JFace that allows us to create a page that is small and knows how to save, restore and apply itself.

This page is used to modify preferences only. They are stored in the preference store that belongs to the main plug-in class. That way, preferences can be accessed directly via the preference store.\vskip .1in 
\subsubsection{Declaration}{
\small public class PreferencePage
\\ {\bf  extends} FieldEditorPreferencePage
\refdefined{.FieldEditorPreferencePage}}
\subsubsection{Constructor summary}{
\begin{verse}
\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.preferences.PreferencePage()}{{\bf PreferencePage()}} \\
\end{verse}
}
\subsubsection{Method summary}{
\begin{verse}

\hyperlink{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.preferences.PreferencePage.init(IWorkbench)}{{\bf init(IWorkbench)}} \\
\end{verse}

   \item{\vskip -.6ex \texttt{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.preferences.exceptions.PeriodLengthTooLong} -- Thrown when the value exceeds a limit (4000 when considering weeks, 1000 when months, 80 years).}

\item{
{\bf  Description}

This method fetches the value for the period starting date for the Basic Code Change Model metric. Value is fetched from the Eclipse preference store.
}
\item{{\bf  Returns} -- 
A Date object representing the starting date for the interval in which to calculate Basic Code Change Model metric. 
}%end item
\item{{\bf  Throws}
  \begin{itemize}
   \item{\vskip -.6ex \texttt{java.text.ParseException} -- This exception is thrown when the string fetched from Eclipse preference store is not parsable as a valid Date.}
  \end{itemize}
}%end item
\end{itemize}
}%end item
\item{ 
\index{getPeriodType()}
\hypertarget{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.preferences.Preferences.getPeriodType()}{{\bf  getPeriodType}\\}
\texttt{public static java.lang.String\ {\bf  getPeriodType}()
\label{it.unisa.sesa.repominer.preferences.Preferences.getPeriodType()}}%end signature
\begin{itemize}
\item{
{\bf  Description}

This method fetches the value of the period type from Eclipse preference store.
}
\item{{\bf  Returns} -- 
A String object representing the period type relative to the Extended Code Change Model metric. 
}%end item
\end{itemize}
}%end item
\end{itemize}
}
}
